GOVERNMENT; ADMINISTRATION AND ORGANIZATION
§ 30.001 COUNCIL-MANAGER FORM OF GOVERNMENT.
   The city is governed by the Council-Manager form of government provided by
the city’s home rule Charter. The powers of the city are vested in the City
Council.
(Prior Code, § 30.001)
Charter reference:
   Similar provisions, see Charter §
2
Statutory reference:
   Cities’ adoption of home rule charters, procedures, effect, see 11 O.S. §§
13-101 et seq.
§ 30.002 TIME OF REGULAR MEETINGS OF THE COUNCIL.
   The Council of the city shall hold a regular meeting at 5:00 p.m. on the
first Tuesday of every month. If such Tuesday shall fall on a holiday, the
regular meeting shall be held on the following Thursday at 5:00 p.m. Adjourned
meetings of the Council shall be convened at such times as determined by the
Council.
(Prior Code, § 30.002) (Ord. 556, passed 9-18-2018)
Statutory reference:
   Open meeting law requirements, see 25 O.S. §§ 301 et seq.
§ 30.003 PLACE OF MEETINGS OF THE COUNCIL.
   Every meeting of the Council shall be held in the City Hall, or at such
other place in the city as the City Council may provide.
(Prior Code, § 30.003)
Charter reference:
   Council to meet at least monthly at times as it may prescribe by ordinance
or otherwise, see Charter §
10
§ 30.004 CALL OF SPECIAL COUNCIL MEETINGS.
   (A)   Special meetings of the City Council may be called by the Mayor or two
Council members. The call for such a meeting shall be in writing, stating the
object and purpose of the meeting and the time of holding the same, and shall
be served personally upon each member of the Council.
   (B)   If all members of the Council are present at any special meeting and
waive the service of such notice, the minutes shall show such fact, and any and
all business coming before the Council may be transacted. When a special
meeting is had upon written call, no business can be transacted except such as
may be stated in the call.
(Prior Code, § 30.004)
Charter reference:
   Mayor or two Council members may call special meetings, see Charter §
10
§ 30.005 CITY MANAGER.
   (A)   City Manager appointment. The Council shall appoint a City Manager for
an indefinite term by a vote of a majority of all its members. It shall choose
him or her solely on the basis of his or her executive and administrative
qualifications with special reference to his or her actual experience in, or
his or her knowledge of, accepted practice in respect to the duties of his or
her office.
   (B)   Duties. The City Manager has such duties as are defined by the Charter
and applicable by ordinance and law.
   (C)   Expenditures. The City Manager shall be allowed, empowered and
authorized to make such purchases in an amount to be set by the City Council
from time to time and less of such items, services, and products as the City
Manager shall deem necessary for the operations, management, and function of
the city without the need for prior Council approval and formal bidding.
(Prior Code, § 30.005) (Ord. 2010-516, passed 8-3-2010; Ord. 2020-566, passed
5-5-2020)
Charter reference:
   City Manager appointment, term, removal, see Charter §
20
   Duties of City Manager, see Charter §
22
§ 30.006 CITY CLERK AND CITY TREASURER.
   (A)   City Clerk; duties. A City Clerk shall be appointed by the City
Council for an indefinite term, and shall be removable by the Council. The City
Clerk is an officer of the city, and has such duties as are prescribed by the
Charter, applicable law, and ordinance.
   (B)   City Treasurer. There shall be a City Treasurer, who is an officer of
the city and who shall be appointed by the Council for an indefinite term.
   (C)   Duties of the City Treasurer. The City Treasurer shall deposit daily
all funds coming into his or her hands in such depositories as the Council may
designate, and shall disburse such funds in the manner provided by applicable
law or ordinance. He or she shall have such other powers, duties, and functions
as may be prescribed by applicable law or by ordinance.
   (D)   City Manager to be ex officio City Treasurer. The duly appointed,
qualified, and acting City Manager is hereby designated and appointed ex
officio City Treasurer, with full power and authority to collect revenue and
other moneys for the city, and to perform all other and further duties, as City
Treasurer, authorized by the Charter, in addition to his or her duties as City
Manager. No further or additional salary or compensation shall be allowed or
paid to the City Manager for his or her services as ex officio City Treasurer.
(Prior Code, § 30.006)
Charter reference:
   Authority of City Manager to hold other positions in city government, see
Charter §
42
   City Clerk, appointment, service as ex officio Treasurer, see Charter §
9
   City Treasurer, see Charter §
25
   City Treasurer; appointment, duties, see Charter §
25
   Service as ex officio or acting Clerk, see Charter §
9
§ 30.007 RETENTION AND DESTRUCTION OF CITY RECORDS.
   (A)   The following records shall be retained for the period indicated
thereafter:
      (1)   Employee retirement records: five years;
      (2)   Employee fire pension records: five years;
      (3)   Sanitation contracts: five years from contract expiration date;
      (4)   Council packets containing agendas and minutes: five years;
      (5)   Employee health insurance: five years;
      (6)   Cafeteria plans: five years;
      (7)   Property and liability insurance: ten years;
      (8)   Workers compensation: ten years;
      (9)   Boyer Lake Dam inspection reports: 15 years;
      (10)   Safety meetings: three years;
      (11)   Golf course receipts: ten years;
      (12)   Golf cart shed rental: two years; and
      (13)   Swimming pool receipts: ten years.
   (B)   The following shall be permanently retained: all Sewer and Water
Improvement District records; all records of City Council meetings, minutes,
ordinances, and resolutions; all WPWA meeting minutes; all election, including,
but not limited to, Charter changes and Council members; all grants that were
obtained for sewer, water, or parks; and all records that are subject to
pending litigation.
   (C)   All other records shall be retained or destroyed at the instruction of
the City Manager, which instruction must be consistent with 11 O.S. § 22-131.
(Prior Code, § 30.007) (Ord. 2009-508, passed 8-4-2009)
OTHER PERSONNEL AND DEPARTMENTS
§ 30.020 DEPARTMENT OF LAW; CITY ATTORNEY.
   There shall be a Department of Law, the head of which is the City Attorney,
appointed by the City Council for an indefinite term, and removable by the
Council. The City Attorney is an officer of the city, and has supervision and
control of the Department of Law. The City Attorney is the chief legal adviser
of the Council and all other officers, departments, and agencies of the city
government in matters relating to their official powers and duties. He or she
represents the city in proceedings in the courts, and performs all services
incident to his or her position which may be required by law or ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 30.020)
Charter reference:
   Department of law, City Attorney, see Charter §
23
§ 30.021 COOPERATIVE HEALTH DEPARTMENT; DIRECTOR.
   The Cooperative Health Department of the county and its Director shall have
the powers of a City Health Department and City Health Officer respectively for
the city. References to HEALTH DEPARTMENT and HEALTH OFFICER or DIRECTOR OF THE
HEALTH DEPARTMENT in this code and in other ordinances of the city means the
Cooperative Health Department and its Director, unless the context clearly
indicates another meaning.
(Prior Code, § 30.021)
§ 30.022 OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES; NUMBER AND CLASSES; COMPENSATION.
   The Council, by motion, resolution, or ordinance, may regulate the number of
classes of offices and positions of employment in the various departments,
offices, and agencies of the city government, and may determine or regulate the
compensation to be paid to officers and employees.
(Prior Code, § 30.022)
§ 30.023 CERTAIN PERSONNEL TO BE BONDED.
   Before entering upon their official duties, the members of the Council, City
Manager, City Treasurer, City Clerk, all officers and employees of the city who
handle money belonging to the city, and all police officers of the city shall
provide bonds for the faithful performance of their official duties, payable to
the city, with a surety company authorized to operate within the state, in such
amount and with such conditions as the Council may prescribe.
(Prior Code, § 30.023) (Ord. 442, passed 7-18-1995)
Charter reference:
   Officer’s bond, see Charter §
43
Statutory reference:
   Bonds of officers, Treasurer to give bond and others defined by ordinance,
see 11 O.S. § 8-105
§ 30.024 CODE ENFORCEMENT OFFICER.
   The Code Enforcement Officer for the city is hereby authorized to issue
citations for violations of the city code. The Code Enforcement Officer for the
city shall carry or display a badge or other emblem of authority as an officer
of the city. Citations issued by the Code Enforcement Officer shall be enforced
and prosecuted in the same manner as such other citations issued by law
enforcement officers for the city.
(Prior Code, § 30.024) (Ord. 2008-504, passed 9-16-2008)
SOCIAL SECURITY
§ 30.035 DECLARATION OF POLICY TO COME UNDER COVERAGE.
   (A)   It is hereby declared to be the policy and purpose of the city to
extend, at the earliest date, to the eligible employees and officials of the
city the benefits of the system of Federal Old-Age and Survivors Insurance as
authorized by the Federal Social Security Act, and all amendments thereto, and
51 O.S. §§ 121 et seq.
   (B)   In pursuance of this policy, the officers and employees of the city
shall take such action as may be required by applicable state or federal laws
or regulations.
(Prior Code, § 30.035)
Statutory reference:
   Social Security coverage for local governments, see 51 O.S.
§ 30.036 EXECUTION OF AGREEMENT WITH STATE AGENCY.
   The Mayor is authorized and directed to execute all necessary agreements and
amendments with the State Department of Human Services to accomplish the
provisions of §
30.035.
(Prior Code, § 30.036)
§ 30.037 WITHHOLDINGS.
   Withholdings from salaries or wages of employees and officials for the
purposes provided in §
30.035 are hereby authorized to be made in the amounts and at such times as may
be required by applicable state and federal laws or regulations, and shall be
paid over to the state or federal agency designated by the laws and
regulations.
(Prior Code, § 30.037)
§ 30.038 CONTRIBUTIONS.
   Employer contributions shall be paid from amounts appropriated for these
purposes from available funds to the designated state or federal agency in
accordance with applicable state or federal laws or regulations.
(Prior Code, § 30.038)
§ 30.039 RECORDS AND REPORTS.
   The city shall keep such records and submit such reports as may be required
by applicable state or federal laws or regulations.
(Prior Code, § 30.039)
§ 30.040 EXCLUSIONS.
   Excluded from this subchapter authorizing the extension of Social Security
benefits to city officers and employees are the following:
   (A)   Any authority to make any agreement with respect to any position,
employee, or official now covered or authorized to be covered by any other
ordinance creating any retirement system for any employee or official of the
city; or
   (B)   Any authority to make any agreement with respect to any position,
employee, or official for which compensation is on a fee basis, or any
position, employee, or official not authorized to be covered by applicable
state or federal laws or regulations.
(Prior Code, § 30.040)
FIRE PENSION SYSTEM
§ 30.055 FUND TO BE OPERATED IN ACCORDANCE WITH LAW.
   The city’s Firefighters’ Pension and Retirement System and Fund shall be
operated in accordance with state law relating to the fund and system.
(Prior Code, § 30.055)
§ 30.056 CONTRIBUTIONS TO FUND.
   (A)   The Clerk shall deduct from the salaries or wages of each paid member
of the Fire Department the amounts which are required by applicable state law.
If the members of the Fire Department, by a majority vote of its paid members,
vote to increase the amount of the deductions, the amounts authorized by this
division (A) shall be increased to reflect the amounts approved by the majority
vote. The Treasurer of the city shall deposit monthly in the State Firefighters
Pension and Retirement Board the amounts deducted pursuant to this division
(A). Any amounts deducted from the salary or wages of a Fire Department member
shall be made at the time of each payroll. The deductions shall be set forth in
the payroll so that each member may be able to ascertain the exact amount which
he or she is contributing.
   (B)   The City Treasurer shall deposit monthly with the State Firefighters
Pension and Retirement Board the amounts of money which are required by
applicable state law for each paid member of the Fire Department.
   (C)   For each volunteer member of the Fire Department, the City Treasurer
shall deposit yearly with the State Firefighters Pension and Retirement Board
the amounts of money which are required by applicable state law. These amounts
may be revised according to actuarial studies and amounts as set by the State
Firefighters Pension and Retirement Board.
   (D)   All assets of the city Firefighters’ Pension and Retirement Fund shall
be transferred to the State Firefighters Pension and Retirement Board. Assets
shall be transferred in the form of cash, negotiable securities, and such other
specific assets as permitted by the State Board.
(Prior Code, § 30.056) (Ord. 383, passed 12-3-1974)
Statutory reference:
   Firefighters pension law, see 11 O.S. § 49-122
EMPLOYEE RETIREMENT SYSTEM
§ 30.070 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   BOARD OF TRUSTEES or BOARD. The Board of Trustees of the employee retirement
system of the city, as created by this subchapter.
   ELECTED OFFICIAL. Any officer duly elected by the citizens of the city.
   EMPLOYEE.
      (1)   Any official or employee of any department of the city, whether
governmental or proprietary in nature, whose employment is of a permanent
nature; provided that elected officials are specifically excluded from the
definition of EMPLOYEE, and provided further that members of the Police and
Fire Departments who are covered by other pension and retirement systems, and
seasonal and part-time employees, are specifically excluded from the definition
of EMPLOYEE.
      (2)   Any person classified as a temporary employee, after serving 12
consecutive months in the employ of the city, shall be included in the
definition of EMPLOYEE.
   RETIREMENT SYSTEM or SYSTEM. The employee retirement system of the city, as
created by this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 30.070)
Charter reference:
   Authority of Council to adopt pension and retirement systems for officers
and employees, see
    Charter §
7(4)
Statutory reference:
   Municipal retirement systems generally, see 11 O.S. §§ 48-101 et seq.
§ 30.071 CREATED; PURPOSE.
   There is hereby authorized and created, pursuant to the provisions of state
law as amended, the employee retirement system of the city for the purpose of
inducing more meritorious and permanent service among employees.
(Prior Code, § 30.071)
§ 30.072 BOARD OF TRUSTEES CREATED.
   For the purpose of managing and administering the retirement system, there
is hereby created a Board of Trustees, which shall be known as the Board of
Trustees of the employee retirement system of the city.
(Prior Code, § 30.072)
§ 30.073 COMPOSITION OF BOARD OF TRUSTEES.
   The Board of Trustees shall consist of five members as follows: the three
members of the City Council, the City Clerk, and the City Treasurer. If any
such officer ceases to hold office, his or her successor shall succeed him or
her as a member of the Board of Trustees.
(Prior Code, § 30.073)
§ 30.074 ELECTION AND TERM OF CHAIRPERSON OF BOARD OF TRUSTEES.
   As soon as the personnel of the Board of Trustees is completed as provided
in this subchapter, it shall meet and elect a Chairperson from its members, who
shall serve for a term of one year, or until his or her successor is elected.
One year from the date of the first organization meeting, and each year
thereafter, the Board shall elect a Chairperson from its members. In the event
any Chairperson ceases to be a member of the Board, it shall elect from its
members a Chairperson to serve the unexpired term.
(Prior Code, § 30.074)
§ 30.075 SECRETARY OF BOARD OF TRUSTEES AND TREASURER OF SYSTEM DESIGNATED.
   The City Clerk shall act as the Clerk and Secretary of the Board of
Trustees. The City Treasurer shall act as the Treasurer of the retirement
system.
(Prior Code, § 30.075)
§ 30.076 MEETING OF BOARD; RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS; QUORUM.
   (A)   The Board of Trustees shall hold monthly meetings on the first Tuesday
of each month and upon call of its Chairperson at such other times as he or she
deems necessary. A majority of the members of the Board may call a meeting at
any time, with or without consent of the Chairperson. The Board shall keep a
record of its proceedings, which record shall be a public record.
   (B)   A majority of all members of the Board shall constitute a quorum and
shall have power to transact business. No funds of the retirement system shall
ever be disbursed for any purpose except upon a vote of a majority of all the
members of the Board, which vote shall be taken by “yeas” and “nays.” The vote
of each member so voting shall be entered upon the proceedings.
(Prior Code, § 30.076)
§ 30.077 GENERAL POWERS OF BOARD.
   The Board of Trustees, in addition to other powers contained in this
subchapter, shall have power to:
   (A)   Compel attendance of witnesses and administer oaths;
   (B)   Provide for payment of all necessary expenses, including actuarial and
necessary services, provided that no compensation shall be made to the members
of the Board;
   (C)   Formulate rules and regulations needed for its guidance in conformity
with the provisions of this subchapter; and
   (D)   Receive and administer, in accordance with the provisions of this
subchapter, any gifts or donations to the retirement system.
(Prior Code, § 30.077)
§ 30.078 FUNDS TO BE PAID TO CITY TREASURER.
   All moneys provided for the retirement system shall be paid over to and
received by the City Treasurer for the use and benefit of the retirement system
as a trust fund.
(Prior Code, § 30.078)
§ 30.079 INVESTMENT OF FUNDS.
   The Board of Trustees shall have the power to invest and reinvest any funds
of the system subject to the restrictions imposed by law upon life insurance
companies in the state. The Board shall have the power to purchase and sell all
securities and investments, provided that the proceeds are used for the purpose
of meeting disbursements for retirement pay and other payments as authorized in
this subchapter, or for the purpose of reinvesting the funds in a more
desirable manner, as heretofore provided.
(Prior Code, § 30.079)
§ 30.080 GROUP ANNUITY CONTRACTS FOR PURPOSE OF PROVIDING BENEFITS.
   The Board of Trustees shall have the power to enter into a group annuity
contract or contracts with any legally licensed insurance company authorized to
do business in the state, for the purpose of providing retirement benefits for
employees, and may amend such contract from time to time and make payment to
such company pursuant to the contract, out of the fund created by
appropriations from the city and contributions by employees, in order to
provide the retirement benefits under the contract.
(Prior Code, § 30.080)
§ 30.081 DUTIES OF CITY ATTORNEY.
   The City Attorney shall be the legal advisor to the Board of Trustees and
shall appear on behalf of the Board in all suits brought by or against the
Board.
(Prior Code, § 30.081)
§ 30.082 CONTRIBUTIONS BY CITY.
   (A)   The City Council may appropriate annually such sum of money as it
deems appropriate to be paid into the fund of the retirement system; provided,
however, that no such appropriation shall exceed 10% of the current annual
salaries of all employees covered by the system. Any appropriation so made
shall be for deferred wages.
   (B)   The account of the retirement system shall be a non-fiscal account,
and it is hereby provided that there is no mandatory requirement upon the part
of the city to make any contribution whatsoever for the benefit of the system.
(Prior Code, § 30.082)
§ 30.083 EMPLOYEE CONTRIBUTIONS GENERALLY.
   (A)   Every employee shall contribute to the retirement system, on a
voluntary basis only, a portion of his or her salary as hereinafter set out,
and shall authorize the City Clerk to deduct such sum from his or her salary,
provided that no employee other than those presently on the retirement rolls
and receiving benefits shall receive any of the benefits provided for in this
subchapter, unless he or she shall have contributed as provided herein. Any
employee who is employed by this city after November 24, 1964, as a condition
of his or her employment, shall agree to contribute to the system as follows:
2% of his or her salary for the calendar years 1964 and 1965. The rate for
future years will be determined by November 1 of each year.
   (B)   (1)   Contributions under this section shall be made by payroll
deductions on and after the effective date of the system.
      (2)   If an employee leaves the service of this city for any reason, all
contributions made by him or her to the system shall be refunded. Each employee
shall designate, in writing, a beneficiary, and upon his or her death, any sum
contributed to the system by the deceased employee shall be paid to the
designated beneficiary.
      (3)   No payment shall be made to the designated beneficiary if the
deceased employee leaves surviving him or her a widow, or child or children
under the age of 18 years, or if the employee, his or her widow, or child or
children have received, or are entitled to receive, any payments under the
terms of this subchapter from the funds of the system.
      (4)   Any refunds made by the system to an employee or his or her
beneficiary shall be with interest as prescribed by the Board of Trustees.
(Prior Code, § 30.083)
§ 30.084 RETURN OF WITHDRAWN CONTRIBUTIONS WHEN EMPLOYEE RETURNS TO CITY
SERVICE.
   If an employee leaves the service of this city and withdraws his or her
contributions previously made to the system, and later returns to the service,
he or she shall deposit, at that time, with the system the amount that he or
she withdrew when he or she left the service. Such amount may be returned in
equal monthly installments, but such payments shall not exceed 36 months.
(Prior Code, § 30.084)
§ 30.085 RETIREMENT AGE.
   All eligible employees may, at their option, retire at the age of 55 years.
(Prior Code, § 30.085)
§ 30.086 RETIREMENT PAY.
   There shall be paid to employees who are eligible to retire, as provided in
this subchapter, retirement pay equal to the amount both he or she and the city
have contributed to the plan, plus interest earned, either in a lump sum or in
monthly payments, as decided by the Board of Trustees at the time of
retirement.
(Prior Code, § 30.086)
§ 30.087 DISABILITY ALLOWANCES.
   If, at any time after becoming a member of the retirement system, an
employee becomes disabled to work and employment with the city has terminated,
all contributions to the retirement system by the employee and the city on his
or her behalf will be paid to the employee.
(Prior Code, § 30.087)
§ 30.088 DEATH BENEFITS.
   In the event of the death of any employee who is a member of the system, the
spouse of such deceased employee, or the designated beneficiary, shall be paid
an amount not to exceed 100% of the contribution of the employee and the city,
plus earned interest.
(Prior Code, § 30.088)
§ 30.089 RIGHTS OF EMPLOYEE LEAVING CITY FOR MILITARY SERVICE.
   Any employee who leaves the service of this city by reason of being
impressed into the military service of the United States of America may
receive, in a lump sum, total contributions made by him or her and by the city
on his or her behalf under this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 30.089)
§ 30.090 PRORATION OF BENEFITS IN EVENT OF INSUFFICIENT FUNDS.
   In the event the funds in the retirement system are insufficient to make
full payment in the amount of retirement benefit allowances to all persons
entitled thereto, such funds shall be prorated among those entitled thereto as
the Board of Trustees may determine to be just and equitable.
(Prior Code, § 30.090)
§ 30.091 FUNDS NOT SUBJECT TO GARNISHMENT, ATTACHMENT, ASSIGNMENT.
   No portion of any funds of the retirement system, either before or after any
order is made by the Board of Trustees for payment to any person entitled to
retirement pay, shall be held, seized, taken, subject to, or detained or levied
on by virtue of any garnishment, attachment, execution, injunction, or other
order or decree or any process or proceeding whatever issued out of or by any
court of this state for the payment or satisfaction, in whole or in part, of
any debt, damage, claim, demand, or judgment against any person entitled to
payment from such funds, nor shall such payments or any claim thereto be
assigned, directly or indirectly. Any attempt to assign or transfer such
payments shall be void. The fund shall be held sacredly in trust.
(Prior Code, § 30.091)
§ 30.092 CERTIFIED LIST OF PERSONS ENTITLED TO BENEFITS; RETIREMENT SYSTEM
BOOK.
   The Board of Trustees shall furnish the City Treasurer a written list,
certified to and signed by the Chairperson and Secretary of the Board and
attested under oath, of all persons entitled to payment out of the funds of the
system, showing the purpose for which such payment is to be made. Such list
shall be furnished the Treasurer at each monthly meeting. The Treasurer
thereupon shall enter a copy of the list upon a book to be kept for such
purpose, which book shall be known as “The Employee Retirement System Book.”
(Prior Code, § 30.092)
§ 30.093 ANNUAL REPORT.
   The Secretary of the Board of Trustees shall report annually, at the time of
the election of officers of the Board, the condition of the retirement system,
the receipts and disbursements thereof, together with a full and complete list
of the beneficiaries of funds in the system and the amount paid to such
beneficiaries.
(Prior Code, § 30.093)

PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION
§ 31.01 CREATED; COMPOSITION; APPOINTMENT; TERMS AND REMOVAL OF MEMBERS.
   There is hereby created a Planning and Zoning Commission of the city. The
Commission shall be composed of five members, who are residents of the city,
nominated by the Mayor and confirmed by the City Council. The Mayor shall be an
ex officio member of the Commission. Each appointed member shall hold office
for such period as is prescribed by the Mayor. Members may be removed by the
Mayor or the City Council only for inefficiency, neglect of duty, or
malefaction in office. Vacancies occurring otherwise than through the
expiration of a term shall be filled only for the unexpired term by the Mayor,
with confirmation by the City Council.
(Prior Code, § 31.01)
Charter reference:
   Authority of Council to appoint members of Planning Commission, see Charter
§
7(6)
Statutory reference:
   Planning Commissions may be established, duties, see 11 O.S. §§ 45-101 et
seq.
§ 31.02 ELECTION AND TERMS OF OFFICE.
   The Planning and Zoning Commission shall elect a Chairperson, a Vice
Chairperson, and a Secretary, and may create and fill such other offices as it
may deem necessary. The term of the Chairperson, Vice Chairperson, and
Secretary shall be one year with eligibility for reelection.
(Prior Code, § 31.02)
§ 31.03 GENERAL POWERS AND DUTIES.
   The Planning and Zoning Commission shall have the power and the duty to
prepare and recommend to the City Council for adoption a comprehensive plan for
the physical development of the city. In conducting its work, the Commission
may consider and investigate any subject matter tending to the development and
betterment of the city and may make such recommendations as it may deem
advisable concerning the adoption thereof to the City Council. The Commission
may prepare and recommend to the City Council for adoption rules and
regulations governing the subdivision of land within the corporate limits of
the city. The Commission shall also act as the Zoning Commission and shall have
the power to prepare and to recommend to the City Council for adoption a zoning
plan to regulate and restrict the height, number of stories, and size of
buildings and other structures, the percentage of lot that may be occupied, the
size of yards, courts, and other open spaces, the density of population and the
location and use of buildings, structures, and land for trade, industry,
residences, and other purposes.
(Prior Code, § 31.03)
§ 31.04 MEETINGS; ADOPTION OF RULES; RECORDS TO BE KEPT.
   (A)   The Planning and Zoning Commission shall hold at least one regular
meeting each quarter, at such times and dates as the Commission shall establish
from time to time.
   (B)   Special meetings shall be held at dates and times specifically set by
the Commission when necessary to respond to the requests and needs of the
citizens of the city and when convenient for any business of the Commission.
   (C)   All meetings shall be open to the public and notice of each meeting
shall be published in accordance with state law. The Commission shall adopt
rules for the transaction of business and shall keep a record of its
regulations, transactions, findings, and determinations, which record shall be
a public record.
(Prior Code, § 31.04) (Ord. 94-434, passed 3-1-1994)
§ 31.05 QUORUM.
   (A)   (1)   At any meeting, a majority of the members of the Planning and
Zoning Commission present shall constitute a quorum for the transaction of
business.
      (2)   No action shall be taken which is binding upon the Commission
unless concurred by not less than a majority of members present at any meeting.
   (B)   If a member of the Planning and Zoning Commission shall be absent from
more than one-half of all the meetings of the Commission held within any period
of four consecutive months, he or she shall thereupon cease to hold office as a
member of the Commission.
(Prior Code, § 31.05) (Ord. 99-456, passed 10-19-1999)
§ 31.06 EMPLOYMENT AND COMPENSATION OF PERSONNEL; AUTHORITY TO INCUR EXPENSES.
   (A)   The Planning and Zoning Commission shall have the power and authority
to employ planners, engineers, attorneys, clerks, and other help deemed
necessary, within the limits of the appropriation fixed by the City Council.
   (B)   The salary and compensation for such services shall be fixed by the
Mayor and Council and shall be paid out of the City Treasury. The Planning and
Zoning Commission may incur necessary expenses within the limits of its
appropriation to carry out its purposes and responsibilities.
(Prior Code, § 31.06)
FIRE DEPARTMENT AND SERVICE
§ 31.20 FIRE DEPARTMENT; CHIEF OF THE DEPARTMENT.
   (A)   (1)   There shall be a Fire Department, the head of which shall be the
Chief of the Fire Department appointed by the City Manager for an indefinite
term.
      (2)   It is the duty of the Fire Department, among others, to extinguish
fires; to rescue persons endangered by fire; to resuscitate, and to administer
first aid to, persons injured in or about burning structures, or elsewhere in
case of an emergency; to promote fire prevention; and, unless otherwise
provided, to enforce all ordinances relating to fires, fire prevention, and
safety of person from fire and explosions in theaters, stores, and other public
buildings.
   (B)   The city’s Fire Department is a volunteer department, consisting of
not more than two full-time, salaried firefighters.
(Prior Code, § 31.20)
Statutory reference:
   Volunteer Fire Departments, see 11 O.S. §§ 29-201 to 29-205
§ 31.21 DUTIES OF THE FIRE CHIEF.
   (A)   The Chief shall be at the head of the Department, subject to the laws
of the state, ordinances of the city, and the rules and regulations adopted in
this subchapter.
   (B)   The Chief shall have the following powers and duties.
      (1)   The Chief shall be responsible for the general condition and
efficient operation of the Department, the training of members, and the
performance of all other duties imposed upon him or her.
      (2)   The Chief may inspect, or cause to be inspected by members of the
Department, the fire hydrants, cisterns, and other sources of water supply at
least twice each year.
      (3)   The Chief shall maintain a library or file of publications on fire
prevention and fire protection and shall make use of it to the best advantage
of all members.
      (4)   The Chief shall make every effort to attend all fires and direct
the officers and members in the performance of their duties.
      (5)   The Chief shall see that the citizens are kept informed on fire
hazards in the community and on the activities of the Department.
      (6)   The Chief shall see that each fire is carefully investigated to
determine its cause, and, in the case of suspicion of incendiarism, shall
notify proper authorities and secure and preserve all possible evidence for
future use in the case.
      (7)   The Chief is authorized to enter any building or premise in the
city at any reasonable hour for the purpose of making inspections and to serve
written notice that the owner or occupant must correct any violations that may
be found.
      (8)   The Chief shall see that complete records are kept of all fires,
inspections, apparatus, and equipment, personnel, and other information of the
Department and shall make reports to the City Manager as he or she may require.
(Prior Code, § 31.21)
§ 31.22 DUTIES OF THE ASSISTANT CHIEF.
   In the absence of the Chief, the Assistant Chief on duty shall command the
Department and be held responsible therefor in all respects with the full
powers and responsibilities of the Chief. The Assistant Chief shall be elected
from among the members of the Fire Department.
(Prior Code, § 31.22)
§ 31.23 COMPANY OFFICERS.
   Company officers shall be selected by the Chief based upon the following
criteria:
   (A)   Knowledge of firefighting;
   (B)   Leadership ability; and
   (C)   Knowledge of firefighting equipment.
(Prior Code, § 31.23)
§ 31.24 SECRETARY-TREASURER.
   (A)   One member elected by the members of the Fire Department shall be a
Secretary-Treasurer.
   (B)   His or her duties shall consist of the following:
      (1)   Calling the roll at the opening of each meeting;
      (2)   Keeping the minutes of each meeting; and
      (3)   Collecting any money due the Department by the members.
(Prior Code, § 31.24)
§ 31.25 NEW MEMBERS.
   New members of the Department shall be appointed by the Chief and shall be
on probation for one year after their appointment. Upon completion of their
probation period, new members must be approved by the majority of the other
members of the Fire Department.
(Prior Code, § 31.25)
§ 31.26 BYLAWS.
   The bylaws of the Department shall include the following.
   (A)   All volunteer Fire Department members are required, when notified, to
respond to alarms of fire and other emergencies.
   (B)   A member is required to be present at all regular meetings, called
meetings, and schools presented for the benefit of the firefighters.
   (C)   At least one regular business meeting of the members shall be held
each month.
   (D)   Any member having two unexcused absences in succession or three
unexcused absences in a period of three months will be dropped from the Fire
Department rolls.
   (E)   Any member leaving the city for an extended period of time is required
to notify the Chief.
   (F)   Any member refusing to attend training classes provided for members of
the Department will be dropped.
   (G)   Any member of the Fire Department may be dropped from the rolls for
the following offenses:
      (1)   Conduct unbecoming a firefighter;
      (2)   Any act of insubordination;
      (3)   Neglect of duty;
      (4)   Any violation of rules and regulations governing the Fire
Department; or
      (5)   Conviction of a felony.
(Prior Code, § 31.26)
§ 31.27 RULES AND REGULATIONS.
   The City Council, by motion or resolution, may adopt and change regulations
relating to the Fire Department, its organization, operation, and compensation.
(Prior Code, § 31.27)
§ 31.28 USE OF FIRE EQUIPMENT; INVENTORY AND REPAIR.
   (A)   (1)   No person shall use any fire apparatus or equipment for any
private purpose, nor shall any person willfully and without proper authority
take away or conceal any article used in any way by the Department.
      (2)   No person shall enter any place where fire apparatus is housed or
handle any apparatus or equipment belonging to the Department unless
accompanied by, or having the special permission of, an officer or authorized
member of the Department.
   (B)   The Chief shall prepare and keep a complete inventory of all property
belonging to the Fire Department, and shall, at the expiration of his or her
term, turn over such inventory and all such property to his or her successor,
together with all books, records, reports, and data of the Department.
   (C)   The Chief shall report to the City Manager any necessary repairs,
alterations, or improvements needed by the Fire Department with an estimate of
their probable cost, and shall superintend the making of the repairs,
alterations, or improvements, and if any apparatus shall become disabled for
immediate use, he or she shall repair the same and report his or her action to
the Council.
(Prior Code, § 31.28) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 31.29 CONTRACTS AUTHORIZED OUTSIDE CITY LIMITS.
   The city is hereby authorized and empowered to enter into contracts or
agreements with individuals, firms, private corporations or associations, or
political subdivisions of the state for fire protection outside the corporate
limits of the city, and to contract to provide fire protection jointly with
other organizations and municipal subdivisions of the state.
(Prior Code, § 31.29)
§ 31.30 CONTRACT TERMS; FEES FOR SERVICES.
   Any contract entered into by the city with an individual owner, firm,
private corporation, or association for outside aid or mutual aid for fire
protection shall provide for the payment by the owner, firm, private
corporation or association, or political subdivision to the city for such fire
apparatus and personnel at a rate as set by the City Council by motion or
resolution.
(Prior Code, § 31.30)
§ 31.31 FIREFIGHTERS SERVING IN REGULAR LINE OF DUTY.
   All firefighters of the Fire Department of the city attending and serving at
fires or doing fire prevention work outside the corporate limits of the city,
as herein provided, shall be considered as serving in their regular line of
duty as fully as if they were serving within the corporate limits of the city.
(Prior Code, § 31.31)
§ 31.32 DEPARTMENT CONSIDERED AGENT OF STATE.
   The Fire Department of the city answering any fire alarm, or call, or
performing any fire prevention services outside the corporate limits of the
city shall be considered as an agent of the state, and acting solely and alone
in a governmental capacity, and the municipality shall not be liable in damages
for any act of commission, omission, or negligence while answering or returning
from any fire, or reported fire, or doing any fire prevention work under and by
virtue of §§
31.29 through
31.31.
(Prior Code, § 31.32)
§ 31.33 RATES FOR RUNS MADE OUTSIDE THE CITY LIMITS.
   Charges for rural fires outside the city limits are as follows, subject to
change at discretion of the City Council from time to time:
 
$250          For the first two trucks for the first hour
$100 per hour For each additional hour
$75           For each additional truck after the first two
Fractional hours in excess of 30 minutes will be billed as a full hour
Charges for foam, when used, is that of the current purchase price of the foam
 
(Prior Code, § 31.33) (Ord. 2009-514, passed 11-17-2009)
§ 31.34 SUBSCRIPTION POLICY.
   (A)   A Fire Department subscription policy be and is hereby established
whereby rates for Fire Department Services rendered in relation to fires
occurring in rural areas outside of the city limits of the city be charged and
that the city hereby establishes said rates for said services as follows.
      (1)   Rural fire dues schedule for members. The following amounts are
subject to change at discretion of the City Council from time to time.
 
Acres Owned and/or Operated Annual Dues
Up to 160                   $50
161 to 320                  $100
321 to 640                  $150
641 to 1,280                $200
1,281 to 2,560              $300
2,561 and over              $400
 
      (2)   Fire Department charges per fire for non-members. The following
amounts are subject to change at discretion of the City Council from time to
time.
 
Rate for first and second truck       $250 for the first hour
Rate for first and second truck after $100 per hour for each additional hour*
first hour
Rate for each additional truck        $75 per hour
Foam (if needed)                      Current market price
*Note: Anything over 30 minutes is considered an additional hour
   
   (B)   The effective date of said rate changes shall be March 4, 2014.
(Prior Code, § 31.34) (Ord. 2014-539, passed 3-18-2014)
POLICE DEPARTMENT
§ 31.45 CHIEF OF POLICE.
   (A)   There shall be a Police Department, the head of which is the Chief of
Police appointed by the City Manager for an indefinite term, and removable by
the Manager.
   (B)   The Chief of Police is an officer of the city, and has supervision and
control of the Police Department.
   (C)   All police officers are officers of the city.
(Prior Code, § 31.45)
Statutory reference:
   Municipal police departments, see 11 O.S. §§ 34-101 et seq.
§ 31.46 DUTIES OF DEPARTMENT.
   It is the duty of the Police Department to apprehend and arrest on view or
on warrant and bring to justice all violators of the ordinances of the city; to
suppress all riots, affrays, and unlawful assemblies which may come to its
knowledge, and generally to keep the peace; to serve all warrants, writs,
executions, and other processes properly directed and delivered to them; to
apprehend and arrest persons violating federal or state law as provided by law,
and to turn them over to proper authorities; and in all respects to perform all
duties pertaining to the office of police officers.
(Prior Code, § 31.46)
§ 31.47 ASSISTANT CHIEF OF POLICE.
   (A)   If desired by the Chief of Police, the Chief of Police may select an
officer from the police officers of the city to serve as the Assistant Chief of
Police.
   (B)   An officer so selected as Assistant Police Chief must be an officer of
the city in good standing, must meet the qualifications as set forth in 11 O.S.
§ 34-102, and shall assist the Chief of Police in the supervision and control
of the Police Department in such manner and under such duties as directed by
the Chief of Police.
   (C)   In the absence of or under the direction of the Chief of Police, the
Assistant Chief shall command the Police Department and shall be held
responsible therefor in all respects with all the full powers and
responsibilities of the Chief of Police in his or her absence.
(Ord. 2023-579, passed 4-4-2023)
§ 31.48 DUTIES OF ASSISTANT CHIEF OF POLICE.
   (A)   The Assistant Chief of Police shall be appointed by the Chief of
Police for an indefinite term and may be removed by the Chief of Police.
   (B)   The Assistant Chief of Police shall perform the administrative duties
as directed by the Chief of Police.
   (C)   The Assistant Chief of Police shall be responsible for normal patrol
duties as well as maintaining a shift schedule as set by the Chief of Police.
(Ord. 2023-579, passed 4-4-2023)
