GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 94.001 GOLF COURSE; GOLF CART STORAGE SHEDS.
   (A)   Charge for golf cart storage sheds. The owner of each golf cart
storage shed maintained at the Lakeside Golf Course shall pay a fee based on
the capacity of the shed, which shall be an amount to be set by the City
Council from time to time per cart per year or any portion thereof for each
year beginning 1992, which shall be fully earned when due. The fee for 1992
shall be due March 15, 1992. The fee for each year thereafter shall be due
January 1 of each year.
(Prior Code, § 94.095)
   (B)   Failure to pay. If any storage shed owner fails to pay the fee or
remove the storage shed by the due date, the city shall have a lien thereon for
the total amount due plus any expenses which may be incurred related thereto,
including, without limitation, the expenses of enforcing the lien, which may be
enforced in accordance with 42 O.S. § 91.
(Prior Code, § 94.096)
(Ord. 92-423, passed 2-4-1992) Penalty, see §
94.999
§ 94.002 WALTERS SKATEBOARD PARK.
   (A)   The City Council deems that it is necessary and expedient to the city
and to the best interests of the city to set the following rules regarding use
of the Walters Skateboard Park Facility.
      (1)   Use this park at your own risk. This is a high risk activity and is
non-supervised. The city does not assume any responsibility for injuries that
may occur during the use of this park.
      (2)   No bicycles permitted.
      (3)   The park is open to all patrons, but it is strongly recommended
that children under ten years of age be accompanied by a parent or guardian,
      (4)   There is no charge to use this facility.
      (5)   Skate park hours: Daily 8:00 a.m. to 10:00 p.m. No usage from 10:01
p.m. to 7:59 a.m. Violators will be prosecuted.
      (6)   Safety gear such as helmets, knee and elbow pads, wrist guards, and
gloves must be worn at all times.
      (7)   No profanity, drugs, alcohol, tobacco products, weapons, or
defacing public property.
      (8)   No glass containers.
      (9)   No motorized equipment allowed (except motorized wheel chairs).
      (10)   Keep noise to a minimum. No loud music.
      (11)   Keep food and drink off skate surface. Use trash receptacles.
      (12)   Use only obstacles put in place by the city. No using trash cans,
makeshift or homemade items as obstacles.
      (13)   Do not use facility if hazardous conditions exist including rain,
snow, or ice.
      (14)   Do not overcrowd facility.
      (15)   Horseplay, fighting, or other destructive behavior prohibited.
   (B)   All skaters and visitors must follow these rules or you will be asked
to leave. This facility is provided for all of you. Keeping it open is
everyone’s responsibility.
   (C)   Report any hazards, unsafe conditions, vandalism, or violators to the
City Hall.
(Prior Code, § 94.160) (Ord. 2008-503, passed 8-19-2008) Penalty, see §
94.999
§ 94.003 CITY SWIMMING POOL.
   (A)   The City Council of the city deem that it is necessary and expedient
to the city and to the best interests of the city to set a new fee structure
for admission to and use of the Walters Public Swimming Pool and to adopt this
section setting such fees, to-wit:
   (B)   The fees to be charged for admission to and use of the Walters Public
Swimming Pool shall be subject to change at the discretion of the City Council
from time to time:
      (1)   Children (18 years of age and under): $2.50;
      (2)   Adults (over 18 years of age): $3;
      (3)   Parties:
         (a)   Twenty-five people or less, two-hour minimum: $45 per hour;
         (b)   Twenty-five people or more, two-hour minimum: $60 per hour; and
         (c)   Extra life guard for each 25 people: $15 per hour.
      (4)   Summer pass: $50; and
      (5)   Family pass: $125 for three and $25 for each additional.
(Prior Code, § 94.170) (Ord. 2015-544, passed 4-21-2015)
§ 94.004 WALTERS TOWER RESERVE.
   (A)   Access. Access to the Walters Tower Reserve property located in Block
90, Addition to Walters, Oklahoma, located between Seventh Street and Nebraska,
Walters, Oklahoma, shall be limited to individuals, businesses, corporations,
or entities for the temporary location of campers, fifth wheels, trailers, or
motor homes for overnight accommodation purposes. The use shall be limited to
no more than 14 consecutive days unless prior written approval is granted by
the City Manager. Permit fees shall be charged for any use or occupancy
permitted hereby.
(Prior Code, § 94.145)
   (B)   Permits; fees. A permit issued by the city shall be required prior to
access to said property. A permit fee in an amount to be set by the City
Council from time to time shall be charged for each night of use by any
individual, business, corporation, or entity for each camper, fifth wheel,
trailer, or motor home caused to be located thereon, provided, that should a
permit issue for a period of seven consecutive nights the permit fee shall be
in the amount in another amount to be set by the City Council from time to time
for the seven consecutive night period.
(Prior Code, § 94.146)
   (C)   Dwelling and camping prohibited. No person shall be permitted to
maintain a temporary or permanent residence on the Walters Tower Reserve at any
time, and no camping shall be permitted thereon.
(Prior Code, § 94.147)
(Ord. 2005-486, passed 6-21-2005; Ord. 2011-522, passed 4-19-2011) Penalty, see
§
94.999
PUBLIC LIBRARY
§ 94.015 PURPOSE.
   It is the desire and intent of the governing body of the city to provide
free public library service to the residents of the city for the benefit of the
city, the state, and the nation.
(Prior Code, § 94.001) (Ord. 403, passed 8-18-1981)
§ 94.016 LIBRARY ESTABLISHED.
   The city public library is hereby established.
(Prior Code, § 94.002) (Ord. 403, passed 8-18-1981)
Statutory reference:
   Municipal libraries, power to establish, see 11 O.S. §§ 31-101 et seq.
§ 94.017 GOVERNING BOARD.
   (A)   The public library shall be governed by a board of five members,
appointed by the Mayor, with the approval of the City Council.
   (B)   Appointments to the Library Board shall be made on the basis of
ability, understanding of the total responsibilities and objectives of public
libraries, and an active interest in the attainment of these goals.
   (C)   All Library Board members shall serve thereon without compensation.
(Prior Code, § 94.003) (Ord. 403, passed 8-18-1981)
§ 94.018 TERM OF OFFICE.
   (A)   The Board members shall hold office as follows: initial appointments
shall be for one-year terms, two-year terms, and two three-year terms.
   (B)   Subsequent appointments shall be for three-year terms, except in the
case of an appointment to fill a vacancy, which appointment shall be for the
remainder of the unexpired term which is vacant.
   (C)   All terms of initial and succeeding appointees shall expire on June 20
of the designated year.
(Prior Code, § 94.004) (Ord. 403, passed 8-18-1981)
§ 94.019 REMOVAL FROM OFFICE.
   Any Board member may be removed by the appointing authority for misconduct,
failure to attend Board meetings, or other neglect of duty.
(Prior Code, § 94.005) (Ord. 403, passed 8-18-1981)
§ 94.020 ELECTION OF CHAIRPERSON; RULES OF THE BOARD.
   (A)   Immediately after the initial appointments and annually thereafter,
the Library Board shall meet and organize by an election of one of its number
as Chairperson, and by the election of such other officers as it deems
necessary.
   (B)   They may adopt such laws, rules, and regulations for their own
guidance and for the government of the library as may be expedient and not
inconsistent with this subchapter and the laws of the state.
(Prior Code, § 94.006) (Ord. 403, passed 8-18-1981)
§ 94.021 APPOINTMENT OF MEMBERS OF THE LIBRARY BOARD; HIRING OF LIBRARIAN;
CONTRACTS; BUDGETS.
   (A)   The members of the Library Board of the city shall be appointed by the
Mayor with the approval of the City Council.
   (B)   The City Manager shall hire the librarian for the city library.
   (C)   All contracts affecting the city library shall be approved by the City
Council.
   (D)   The budget for the city library shall be approved by the City Council.
(Prior Code, § 94.007) (Ord. 403, passed 8-18-1981; Ord. 2002-472, passed 9-3-
2002; Ord. 2002-473, passed 9-17-2002)
§ 94.022 ANNUAL FINANCIAL REPORT.
   (A)   The Library Board shall submit an annual financial and statistical
report to the Mayor and City Council and the State Department of Libraries for
each fiscal year ending June 30.
   (B)   The report shall include an accounting for moneys received and
expended and such other statistics about library use, collections, and staff
which may be deemed necessary to account for their trust.
(Prior Code, § 94.008) (Ord. 403, passed 8-18-1981)
§ 94.023 ANNUAL APPROPRIATIONS.
   The Mayor and City Council shall annually appropriate to the Library Board
from funds available to the city such moneys as are deemed necessary to operate
and maintain the city public library for the education and cultural enrichment
of the citizens of the city.
(Prior Code, § 94.009) (Ord. 403, passed 8-18-1981)
CEMETERIES
§ 94.035 CEMETERY ASSOCIATION.
   (A)   A board is hereby established, to be known as the Walters Cemetery
Association. It shall consist of five Trustees, to be appointed and removed by
the Mayor with the approval of the City Council. One Trustee shall be
Chairperson, one Vice Chairperson, and one Secretary whose terms shall expire
July 31 of each year.
   (B)   In July of each year, the members of the Board shall elect their
officers for the next ensuing fiscal year. Trustees shall be appointed to serve
terms of five years, and terms of office shall be staggered at one-year
intervals; provided, however, that the terms of the existing Trustees shall
continue as originally appointed pursuant to Ord. 94-437 in 1994, that is: one
member shall serve a term of two years, one member shall serve a term of four
years, and one member shall serve a term of six years. Of the new Trustees, one
member shall be appointed to a term expiring July 31, 1998, and the other to a
term expiring July 31, 2000. A majority of all the members of the Cemetery
Association shall constitute a quorum. The Association shall hold quarterly
meetings, at such times and places as it shall select, and special meetings as
the Association Chairperson shall deem necessary. A complete copy of the
minutes of each meeting shall be kept by the City Clerk.
(Prior Code, § 94.020) (Ord. 94-437, passed 5-17-1994; Ord. 96-446, passed 11-
5-1996)
§ 94.036 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ASSOCIATION. The Walters Cemetery Association.
   DEPARTMENT. The Parks and Recreation Department of the city.
   RULES AND REGULATIONS. The rules and regulations established by the
Association for cemetery operations.
   SUPERINTENDENT. The person employed as caretaker for the cemeteries owned
and operated by the city.
(Prior Code, § 94.021) (Ord. 94-437, passed 5-17-1994)
§ 94.037 ASSOCIATION AUTHORITY AND POWERS.
   (A)   The Association shall function as both an advisory and administrative
body.
   (B)   It shall have the power to:
      (1)   Adopt rules and regulations for cemetery operations;
      (2)   Make rulings on the applicability of rules and regulations for the
cemetery;
      (3)   Make recommendations affecting cemetery management to the City
Manager;
      (4)   Make recommendations to the City Council for budgetary items;
      (5)   Make recommendations to the City Council with respect to the
employment of a Superintendent; and
      (6)   Set fees and charges for spaces and services rendered at city’s
cemeteries.
(Prior Code, § 94.022) (Ord. 94-437, passed 5-17-1994)
§ 94.038 CEMETERY OWNERSHIP.
   The city shall own the municipal cemeteries, i.e., Walters Cemetery and
Hillside Cemetery, and all other land hereafter acquired by the city for use as
a cemetery.
(Prior Code, § 94.023) (Ord. 94-437, passed 5-17-1994)
§ 94.039 RULES AND REGULATIONS.
   The Association shall have the power to make rules and regulations for the
city’s cemeteries, concerning lots, deeds, plats, monuments, and fees which
shall become effective after approval of the Council.
(Prior Code, § 94.024) (Ord. 94-437, passed 5-17-1994)
§ 94.040 SUPERINTENDENT.
   (A)   The Association shall recommend to the City Council a person or
persons to be considered for employment as the Cemetery Superintendent for the
city.
   (B)   The Superintendent’s duties shall be to officially manage the
cemeteries under the direction of the City Manager and to enforce the rules and
regulations adopted by the Association.
   (C)   The cemeteries shall be included within the Parks and Recreation
Department.
(Prior Code, § 94.025) (Ord. 94-437, passed 5-17-1994)
§ 94.041 LOT CONVEYANCE.
   (A)   Lots in the cemetery shall be conveyed by certificate or deed signed
by the Chairperson of the Association and attested by the Secretary of the
Association, under the seal of the city.
      (1)   The certificate shall show the price for which the lots are sold
and specify that the person to whom it is issued is the owner of the lot or
lots described therein by number, as laid down in the plat, for the purpose of
interment.
      (2)   The certificate shall vest in the purchaser and his or her heirs a
right to the lot or lots, for the sole purpose of interment, under the
regulations of the Association and city.
   (B)   Before recording any conveyance between purchasers and sellers, proof
of ownership and documentation of lot conveyance, as required by the city,
shall be submitted to the City Clerk.
(Prior Code, § 94.026) (Ord. 94-437, passed 5-17-1994)
§ 94.042 RECORDS OF OWNERSHIP.
   The City Clerk shall maintain full and complete records of ownership of all
lots and spaces in the cemetery, of the burial capacity of each lot, whether
sold and unsold, of the location of each grave, of the name of the person
buried in each grave that has been or shall thereafter be used, and of the
burial of each.
(Prior Code, § 94.027) (Ord. 94-437, passed 5-17-1994)
§ 94.043 ABANDONMENT.
   (A)   The city will deem a lot or space abandoned by its owner if:
      (1)   The space or lot has not been used during the past 70 years; and
      (2)   No contact or indication of interest has been shown by the owners
of the space or lot.
   (B)   If a space or lot has been abandoned, it may be reclaimed by the city
using the following procedure:
      (1)   One publication of notice in a newspaper of general circulation in
the city of the city’s intent to reclaim the space or lot described by its deed
or cemetery description; and
      (2)   Attempt to contact the person(s) or heirs of the person(s) shown to
be the legal owner(s) of the cemetery space or lot to ascertain whether he or
she desires to use the space or lot or sell it.
   (C)   After the procedure outlined in division (B) above is completed
without response from the owner(s) or his or her heirs within 30 days of the
publication date, the space or lot may be reclaimed by the city and sold.
   (D)   If an abandoned space or lot is resold and a person appears with a
deed or other reliable proof showing ownership to the space or lot, the
Association and the city shall make another space or lot available to him or
her as a substitute at no additional charge.
   (E)   No space or lot held in trust pursuant to 11 O.S. § 26-104 shall be
considered abandoned.
(Prior Code, § 94.028) (Ord. 94-437, passed 5-17-1994; Ord. 95-440, passed 6-6-
1995) Penalty, see §
94.999
§ 94.044 FUNDS; COLLECTION AND ACCOUNTING.
   (A)   General Care Fund. The General Care Fund shall be comprised of 87.5%
of all money received from the sale of lots and interments plus all donations
specifically designated to this fund by the donor. If no such designation is
made by the donor, a gift in an amount to be set by the City Council from time
to time or less shall be deposited in the General Care Fund. Sums of more than
an amount to be set by the City Council from time to time, but less than
another amount to be set by the City Council from time to time, may be placed
in the General Care Fund if necessary for cemetery operating expenses. Both the
principal and interest generated by the General Care Fund shall be utilized for
the day-to-day operations and maintenance of cemeteries owned by the city. The
City Council shall administer the General Care Fund with due consideration to
the recommendations presented by the Association.
(Prior Code, § 94.029)
   (B)   Permanent Care Fund. The Permanent Care Fund shall be a separate
account comprised of 12.5% of all money received from the sale of lots and
interments plus all un-designated donations that are not deposited with the
General Care Fund pursuant to division (A) above. The fund principal shall be
used to purchase additional cemetery land and to make capital improvements in
the cemetery. The balance of the fund may be invested in the manner provided by
law for the investment of municipal funds. Interest from the investments shall
be used for the same purpose as the principal or to construct lots, walks,
drives, or parks, or to purchase necessary cemetery equipment. The fund shall
be administered by the City Council with due consideration to the
recommendations of the Association.
(Prior Code, § 94.030)
   (C)   Deposit and accounting. It is the duty of the Superintendent, or other
city officials as designated by the City Council, to account for all money
received from the sale of lots or from interments, or from any other source,
and to deposit such funds with the city in the appropriate accounts as outlined
in this subchapter. The city shall make provision and separate accounting in
its yearly budget for operation and maintenance of the cemetery.
(Prior Code, § 94.031)
(Ord. 94-437, passed 5-17-1994)
Statutory reference:
   Cemetery Care Fund, see 11 O.S. § 26-109
§ 94.045 REPORTS.
   The Superintendent shall make a report on the condition of the cemetery at
each Association meeting. An annual written report shall be presented to the
Association in July of each year with all information necessary for
recommending the amount that should be requested for the cemetery budget.
Further, the Association shall, on the first Monday in January and July of each
year, make a full report to the City Council of all lots sold, interments made,
and all money received and expended by the Association.
(Prior Code, § 94.032) (Ord. 94-437, passed 5-17-1994)
§ 94.046 CONCRETE CURBING IN OR AROUND LOTS.
   (A)   Permit. All persons desiring to construct concrete curbing in and
around cemetery lots shall first apply to the Superintendent in charge of the
cemetery and obtain a permit therefor.
(Prior Code, § 94.033)
   (B)   Specifications. All concrete curbing in or around cemetery lots must
be at least six inches in depth and 14 inches in width and shall not extend
above the ground grade or level. Such curbing must also contain four, one-half
inch rebars running parallel to each other.
(Prior Code, § 94.034)
(Ord. 94-437, passed 5-17-1994) Penalty, see §
94.999
LAKE BOYER
§ 94.060 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   LAKE. The body of water owned by the city and known as Lake Boyer. Such term
shall also include all property surrounding the lake and owned or controlled by
the city, unless clearly indicated to the contrary.
   WATER SKIING or SKIING. The act of being towed by boat and motor on properly
designed wooden or metal skis, wherein the person being towed holds or secures
to his or her person a towline direct from the boat.
(Prior Code, § 94.045)
§ 94.061 POLLUTING OR LITTERING.
   It is unlawful for any person to leave or deposit in the lake or on the lake
property any substance or refuse which may tend to pollute the waters of the
lake, or to leave or deposit any cans or rubbish thereon.
(Prior Code, § 94.046) Penalty, see §
94.999
§ 94.062 WADING.
   It is unlawful for any person to wade in the lake, unless he or she is
wearing rubber boots that will not leak, or to wade in water that will come
over the boot tops.
(Prior Code, § 94.047) Penalty, see §
94.999
§ 94.063 SWIMMING.
   (A)   It is unlawful for any person to swim in the lake.
   (B)   This section shall not apply to a person skiing on the lake in accord
with the provisions of this subchapter, while he or she is making a reasonable
and uninterrupted attempt to regain his or her skis or boat, or both, but in
the event that an uninterrupted attempt is not made to do so, such person shall
be in violation of this section.
(Prior Code, § 94.048) Penalty, see §
94.999
§ 94.064 HUNTING AND FISHING.
   (A)   No person shall fish or hunt on the lake or lake property without
first securing a permit therefor from the City Clerk and paying such fees as
may, from time to time, be prescribed by the City Council. No free permits
shall ever be issued.
   (B)   No game, except migratory birds, shall be killed upon the lake or lake
property.
   (C)   No fishing shall be allowed in the lake, except at such times as the
same may be recommended by the State Fish and Game Commission.
   (D)   It is unlawful for any person to exceed the limit, as to size and
number, of fish taken from the lake, as such limit is fixed by the State Fish
and Game Commission.
(Prior Code, § 94.049) Penalty, see §
94.999
§ 94.065 WHEN OPERATION OF BOATS PERMITTED.
   (A)   Boats propelled by a motor of ten or less horsepower may be operated
on the lake from sunup to sundown on any day.
   (B)   Boats propelled by a motor of more than ten horsepower may be operated
on the lake on any Sunday or Wednesday between 1:00 p.m. and sundown. Such
boats may also be operated, for the purpose of towing skiers, at any time that
skiing is permitted by §
94.068.
   (C)   Boats which are not propelled by a motor may be operated on the lake
on any day between sunup and 11:00 p.m.
   (D)   It is unlawful for any person to operate any boat on the lake, except
during the times that such operation is permitted by this section.
(Prior Code, § 94.050) Penalty, see §
94.999
§ 94.066 BOATS, REGULATIONS FOR USE.
   (A)   Permits for motorboats.
      (1)   No person shall operate any motor boat on the lake, unless a
current permit has been issued for such boat by the City Clerk. No such permit
shall be issued unless the boat is in compliance with all applicable provisions
of this subchapter.
      (2)   (a)   An annual boat permit, valid for the calendar year, may be
obtained upon payment of a fee as set by the Council, by motion or resolution,
for boats propelled by a motor of more than ten horsepower, or boats propelled
by a motor of ten horsepower or less.
         (b)   A daily permit, valid only for the day for which issued, may be
obtained for a boat propelled by a motor of more than ten horsepower, upon
payment of a fee as set by the Council.
(Prior Code, § 94.051)
   (B)   Boats to be equipped with floats. It is unlawful for any person to
operate or maintain any character of boat in and upon the waters of the lake,
for pleasure, fishing, or any other purpose, without first providing such boat
with at least two air chambers or floats of such size and capacity and with
sufficient buoyancy to keep such boat afloat under all reasonable circumstances
and conditions of the weather.
(Prior Code, § 94.052)
   (C)   Boat operation while intoxicated or under influence of drugs; reckless
operation. It is unlawful for any person to operate any boat, motorboat, or any
other type of watercraft on the lake while under the influence of intoxicating
liquor or narcotics or other habit-forming drugs, or to operate any boat,
motorboat, or any other type of watercraft on the lake in a careless, wanton,
or reckless manner so as to endanger the life or property of another.
(Prior Code, § 94.053)
   (D)   Speed limit for boats near shore or dam. It is unlawful for any person
to operate any motorboat on the lake at a speed in excess of five mph when such
boat is within 200 feet of the shoreline or 300 feet of the dam.
(Prior Code, § 94.054)
Penalty, see §
94.999
§ 94.067 CITY NOT LIABLE FOR DAMAGES RESULTING FROM ACTIVITIES AT LAKE.
   The city shall not be liable, by reason of the provisions of this subchapter
or the issuance of any license or permit hereunder, for damages resulting from
injury to persons or property or loss of life, and any person operating any
boat or occupying any boat as a passenger, or otherwise using the lake or lake
property, shall do so solely at his or her own risk and responsibility.
(Prior Code, § 94.055) Penalty, see §
94.999
§ 94.068 WATER SKIING, WHEN AND WHERE PERMITTED.
   (A)   Water skiing shall be permitted upon Lake Boyer, between May 30 and
September 30 of each year, each day between the hours of 1:00 p.m. and sundown.
It is unlawful for any person to ski upon the lake at any other time.
   (B)   The skiing area upon the lake shall be in and upon the main body of
water 300 feet from the dam and 200 feet from the remaining surrounding
shoreline. Skiing nearer to the dam than 300 feet or the shoreline than 200
feet is prohibited, except from the takeoff point and incoming point upon the
shore to the skiing area.
   (C)   No person shall ski in the sloughs of the lake.
(Prior Code, § 94.056) Penalty, see §
94.999
§ 94.069 WATER SKIING, REGULATIONS FOR USE.
   (A)   License.
      (1)   It is unlawful for any person to ski on the lake, unless he or she
has a current license to do so issued by the City Clerk.
      (2)   A seasonal license, valid from May 30 through September 30 of the
year in which issued, may be obtained under this section, upon payment of a fee
as set by the Council by motion or resolution. If a person holds such a
seasonal license, other members of his or her immediate family living in his or
her home may obtain a similar license upon payment of a fee as set by the
Council for each such license.
      (3)   A daily license, valid only for the day for which issued, may be
obtained under this section, upon payment as set by the Council.
(Prior Code, § 94.057)
   (B)   Minimum length of skis; skis to be easily removed. Skis used on the
lake shall be not less than five feet in length, and shall be constructed so as
to permit easy removal. Skis available on the commercial market shall be deemed
to comply with this section.
(Prior Code, § 94.058)
   (C)   Minimum length of towline. Any line or rope used to tow a skier on the
lake shall be at least 30 feet in length.
(Prior Code, § 94.059)
   (D)   Life jackets. It is unlawful for any person to ski on the lake, or to
operate or ride in a boat towing a skier, unless he or she is wearing a
regulation life jacket.
(Prior Code, § 94.060)
   (E)   Boat not to tow more than two skiers. Not more than two skiers shall
be towed on the lake by the same boat at the same time.
(Prior Code, § 94.061)
   (F)   Towboat meeting or passing other boats. Boats towing skiers on the
lake shall keep to the right of other boats approaching from the opposite
direction and shall pass to the left of other boats proceeding in the same
direction.
(Prior Code, § 94.062)
Penalty, see §
94.999
SULTAN PARK
§ 94.080 VEHICLES.
   (A)   Speed. No vehicle shall be driven in Sultan Park at a greater speed
than 15 mph at all times.
(Prior Code, § 94.110)
   (B)   Driving on roadways. All vehicles shall be driven only on designated
roadways. No off-road driving shall be permitted.
(Prior Code, § 94.113)
   (C)   Parking. All vehicles shall be permitted to park off-road.
(Prior Code, § 94.114)
   (D)   Permitted vehicles. Only the operation of registered vehicles shall be
permitted. All non-registered vehicles (including four-wheelers, but excluding
bicycles) shall be prohibited.
(Prior Code, § 94.115)

which launch any type of projectile, be permitted in Sultan Park.

§ 94.083 ACTS PROHIBITED.
   The following acts in Sultan Park are prohibited:
   (A)   Jumping or diving from the bridges or dock;
   (B)   Swimming or wading (including fishing waders);
   (C)   Camping without a permit;
   (D)   Fishing without a state fishing license;
   (E)   Littering;
   (F)   Operating any type of motorized water craft on the waterways
(excluding toy boats);
   (G)   Operating any vehicle on the swinging bridge;
   (H)   Molesting the goldfish;
   (I)   Use of glass bottles or glass containers; and
   (J)   The taking of bait fish in the Ox Bow pond, by any means, is
prohibited.
(Prior Code, § 94.116) (Ord. 2004-482, passed 6-18-2004; Ord. 2011-524, passed
9-6-2011) Penalty, see §
94.999
§ 94.084 FIREWORKS.
   No fireworks of any kind shall be discharged at Sultan Park, except on the
date designated by the City Manager, for the official celebration of
Independence Day each year, and only inside an area described as follows:
between the western most internal road of Sultan Park to the county road
bordering Sultan Park on the west side of the park; from the southern bottom
edge of the berm on the south side of the softball field southerly to the road
which serves as the western exit of Sultan Park; from the road which serves as
the western exit of Sultan Park southerly to the ditch which forms the southern
boundary of Sultan Park at that point; and from a point 50 feet west of the
gold fish pond to the county road bordering Sultan Park on the west side of the
park, and that said area shall be clearly marked so that all persons can
identify said area.
(Prior Code, § 94.117) (Ord. 2005-485, passed 5-17-2005) Penalty, see §
94.999
WALTERS YOUTH PARK AND KIDTOPIA PLAYGROUND FACILITY
§ 94.095 ACCESS TO WALTERS YOUTH PARK.
   (A)   Access to the Walters Youth Park located on East Kansas Street shall
be prohibited between the hours of 11:00 p.m. and 5:00 a.m. during the week
(Monday through Thursday) and 12:00 a.m. and 5:00 a.m. on weekends (Friday
through Sunday) for children under the age of 18 years, except as follows.
      (1)   Attendance at properly supervised practices or games of little
league softball, baseball, football, or other sports shall be permitted until
such practices or games are concluded.
      (2)   Use of the basketball courts for practices or games and the tennis
courts for practice or matches shall be permitted until such practices, games,
or matches are concluded.
   (B)   The City Council deems that it is necessary and expedient to the city
and to the best interests of the city to set the following rules regarding use
of the Walters Youth Park.
      (1)   Use this park at your own risk. This is a high risk activity and is
non-supervised. The city does not assume any responsibility for injuries that
may occur during the use of this park.
      (2)   The park is open to all patrons, but it is strongly recommended
that children under ten years of age be accompanied by a parent or guardian.
      (3)   There is no charge to use this facility.
      (4)   Hours: daily from 5:00 a.m. to 12:00 a.m. No use from 12:01 a.m. to
5:00 a.m. Violators will be prosecuted.
      (5)   No smoking in park. Smoking is permitted in the parking lot only.
      (6)   No profanity, drugs, alcohol, tobacco products, or weapons shall be
allowed on the premises.
      (7)   Defacing public property is prohibited.
      (8)   No glass containers are allowed on the premises.
      (9)   Motorized equipment is not allowed on the premises including ATVs,
go-carts, golf carts, scooters, dirt bikes, or any other motor driven
recreational vehicles (except motorized wheel chairs).
      (10)   Keep noise to a minimum. No loud music.
      (11)   Gates shall be secured at all times.
      (12)   No hanging from basketball rims.
      (13)   All trash must be picked up. The use of trash receptacles is
required.
      (14)   Do not use facility if hazardous conditions exist.
      (15)   Vehicles are allowed in designated areas only.
      (16)   Horseplay, fighting, or other destructive behavior is prohibited.
      (17)   No open fires, fire pits, or any other burning is permitted.
      (18)   Guests, parents, or others interfering with a youth game will be
ejected or banned from park.
      (19)   Drunkards and all persons who have consumed alcohol prior to
coming to the Youth Park are not allowed on the premises.
      (20)   All visitors must follow these rules or you will be asked to
leave. Those who violate these rules will be prosecuted. Where applicable,
fines will be imposed for violation of these rules. This facility is provided
for all of you; keeping it open is everyone’s responsibility.
      (21)   Report any hazards, unsafe conditions, vandalism, or violators to
the City Hall at 129 E. Colorado, 8:00 a.m. to 5:00 p.m. Monday through Friday:
875-3337. After hours: Call Central Dispatch at 580-875-6061. Weekends,
holidays: 875-2060. Emergency: 911. Ambulance: 911.
(Prior Code, § 94.130) (Ord. 2003-480, passed 11-14-2003; Ord. 2011-529, passed
12-20-2011) Penalty, see §
94.999

   Access to and use of the Kidtopia Playground Facility shall be permitted
only for children 12 years of age or under and only with proper supervision by

access to the Kidtopia Playground Facility shall be governed by the terms of §
94.095.

§ 95.01 PLANTS, SHRUBS PROHIBITED WHEN A TRAFFIC HAZARD.
   No owner or occupant of any lot or parcel of land in the city shall allow or
permit any tree, shrub, or plant, or any fence, wall, sign, or billboard,
building, or other object to grow or to be built or moved upon the street or
alley right-of-way abutting such lot or parcel of ground when the same shall
constitute a traffic hazard by obstructing the view of any vehicle on any
street of the city.
(Prior Code, § 95.01) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.02 UNLAWFUL TO INJURE TREES AND SHRUBBERY.
   It is unlawful for any person to injure any tree or shrubbery on a street or
alley in the city. This section shall not prohibit the lawful and proper care
and removal of such trees and shrubbery.
(Prior Code, § 95.02) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.03 UNLAWFUL TO OBSTRUCT SIDEWALKS, PARKWAYS, STREETS, AND ALLEYS WITH
MERCHANDISE.
   Except when otherwise proclaimed as lawful by public proclamation of the
Mayor of the city, it is unlawful for any person to place upon or permit to be
placed upon the sidewalks, parkways, streets, and alleys of the city any goods,
wares, articles of merchandise, or any other obstruction, and leave same
thereon; or to use the same as a place to display goods or to carry on a
business or trade.
(Prior Code, § 95.03) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.04 UNLAWFUL TO OBSTRUCT UNDULY SIDEWALKS AND STREETS.
   It is unlawful for any person to use or obstruct the sidewalks of the city
in any manner so as to interfere unduly with pedestrian traffic thereon, or to
use or obstruct the streets and alleys of the city in any manner so as to
interfere unduly with lawful traffic and parking thereon.
(Prior Code, § 95.04) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.05 UNLAWFUL TO DEPOSIT TRASH UPON STREETS OR SIDEWALKS.
   It is unlawful for any person to deposit, throw, or sweep into or upon a
street, alley, parking, or sidewalk of the city any paper, rubbish, grass,
weeds, tree trimmings, dirt, trash, crates, boxes, or other refuse of any kind,
except as may be specifically authorized in this code.
(Prior Code, § 95.05) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.06 OWNER OR OCCUPANT NOT TO PERMIT SIDEWALK OR SIDEWALK AREA TO BECOME A
HAZARD.
   It is unlawful for the owner or occupant of property abutting upon a
sidewalk or sidewalk area to permit the sidewalk or sidewalk area adjacent to
the property to become a hazard to persons using the sidewalk or sidewalk area.
(Prior Code, § 95.06) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.07 CERTAIN OBSTRUCTIONS PROHIBITED.
   (A)   No person may obstruct any street, avenue, alley, crosswalk, sidewalk,
right-of-way, easement, or public ground in the city by any one of the
following:
      (1)   Placing, erecting, constructing, or maintaining any structure over,
upon, or across any such area or by placing any bush, hedge, or fence on such
area or by blocking by any means except as authorized in this code;
      (2)   Parking or working on any automobile, truck, motorcycle, or other
vehicle which is not in a condition to be operated in its normal manner of
operation or which is partially dismantled or is in the process of or is
completely dismantled or junked, except minor emergency repairs; and/or
      (3)   Parking, from sunset to sunrise, any truck, tractor, trailer, or
other vehicle having dual wheels, or the chassis thereof, any boat trailer,
motor home, or camping trailer of any size, or any vehicle having a width
greater than 84 inches within the area of the city zoned as R-1 Single-R Family
Residential District and R-2 Mixed Residential District.
   (B)   Any of the acts hereby prohibited shall constitute an obstruction even
though it is only a partial obstruction of the public’s free and unrestricted
use of such street, avenue, alley, crosswalk, sidewalk, right-of-way, easement,
or other public ground.
(Prior Code, § 95.07) (Ord. 97-450, passed 10-7-1997) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.08 DISPLAY OF ADDRESS.
   All owners of residential and business structures located in the city shall
cause the street address numbers of such structures to be displayed in a manner
so that such numbers are clearly visible from the street. Such numbers shall be
a minimum of three inches and a maximum of six inches in height, shall be a
maximum one and one-half inches in width, and must be located on or near the
structure.
(Prior Code, § 95.08) (Ord. 2003-475, passed 6-3-2003) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Any person, firm, or corporation violating any provision of §
95.01 shall be deemed guilty of an offense against the city and shall, upon
conviction thereof, be punished as provided in §
10.99; however, no party shall be deemed to be in violation thereof until and
unless he or she has had notice by certified mail of such purported traffic
hazard and has failed to abate such hazard during the ten days next succeeding
receipt of such notice.
(Prior Code, § 95.01)
   (C)   Failure to display the street address number of a structure, as
required in §
95.08, shall be a violation hereof punishable in accordance with §§
10.99 and
32.29.
(Prior Code, § 95.08)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 110.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purposes of this chapter, all words, phrases, and terms used in this
chapter and not defined herein shall be interpreted and construed in conformity
with the definitions of the same set forth in 37A O.S. § 1-103, with the same
force and effect as if set forth in full herein, and such definitions are made
a part hereof by reference.
(Prior Code, § 110.01) (Ord. 95-443, passed 11-21-1995)
§ 110.02 UNLAWFUL RECEIPT; POSSESSION; SALE.
   (A)   No person shall receive, possess, sell, barter, give away,
manufacture, or use any alcoholic beverages in violation of the constitution
and statutes of the state or the ordinances of the city.
   (B)   No person holding a license or permit under 37A O.S. §§ 1-101 et seq.,
the state Alcoholic Beverage Control Act, shall receive, possess, or sell any
alcoholic beverages, except as authorized by law and by the state license or
permit which he or she holds.
   (C)   It is unlawful for any person, firm, or corporation, or any agent or
employee thereof, to keep, maintain, or aid or abet in keeping or maintaining,
a place where any alcoholic beverage is manufactured, sold, bartered, given
away, or otherwise furnished in violation of law.
(Prior Code, § 110.02) (Ord. 95-443, passed 11-21-1995) Penalty, see §
110.99
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see 37A O.S. § 6-101
§ 110.03 LOITERING ON PREMISES USED FOR ILLEGAL SALE.
   It is unlawful for any person to loiter in any place where alcoholic
beverages of any kind are bartered, sold, given away, or otherwise furnished
contrary to law.
(Prior Code, § 110.03) (Ord. 95-443, passed 11-21-1995) Penalty, see §
110.99
§ 110.04 TO BE PURCHASED ONLY FROM LICENSED DEALERS.
   No person shall buy any alcoholic beverages, either at retail or wholesale,
from any person other than a dealer licensed under the laws of the state.
(Prior Code, § 110.04) (Ord. 95-443, passed 11-21-1995) Penalty, see §
110.99
§ 110.05 PACKAGE STORE OCCUPATION TAX.
   (A)   There is hereby levied upon each person holding a lawful license
issued by the State Alcoholic Beverage Control Board for the operation of a
retail package store within the corporate limits of the city an annual
occupation tax in the maximum amount allowed by state law, as it may be amended
from time to time.
   (B)   All occupation taxes levied under the provisions of this section shall
expire on June 30 of each year, and shall be computed pro rata upon the months
remaining in the year ending June 30. Such taxes paid on or before the
fifteenth of any month shall be on the basis of the first day of each month,
and such taxes paid after the fifteenth day of any month shall be on the basis
of the first day of the next succeeding month.
   (C)   No retail package store shall be operated in the city until the
occupation tax levied by this section has been paid in full to the City Clerk
and his or her receipt has been issued therefor. The City Clerk shall make and
transmit to the State Alcoholic Beverage Control Board an annual report showing
the number of licenses upon which occupation taxes were levied under this
section, and the amount of money collected from such taxes.
(Prior Code, § 110.05) (Ord. 95-443, passed 11-21-1995) Penalty, see §
110.99
Statutory reference:
   Authority to levy above tax, see 37A O.S. § 4-104
§ 110.06 PACKAGE STORE PREMISES TO BE SEPARATED FROM PREMISES WHERE OTHER
BUSINESS CONDUCTED.
   Except as may be permitted by state law, no retail package store shall be
conducted upon any premises, unless such premises are separated from the
premises on which any other goods, wares, or merchandise are sold or services
are rendered by non-transparent walls, which may be broken by a passageway to
which the public is not admitted. It is unlawful for any person to take any
alcoholic beverage from such store through such passageway for the purpose of
selling, reselling, or delivering in connection with the sale of such alcoholic
beverage.
(Prior Code, § 110.06) (Ord. 95-443, passed 11-21-1995) Penalty, see §
110.99
§ 110.07 SALE OR DELIVERY TO MINORS.
   No person shall knowingly sell, deliver, or furnish any alcoholic beverage
to any person under 21 years of age.
(Prior Code, § 110.07) (Ord. 95-443, passed 11-21-1995) Penalty, see §
110.99
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see 37A O.S. § 6-101A.1.
§ 110.08 MINORS NOT TO MISREPRESENT AGE FOR PURPOSE OF BUYING.
   No persons under 21 years of age shall misrepresent his or her age in
writing or by presenting false documentation of age for the purpose of inducing
any person to sell him or her alcoholic beverages.
(Prior Code, § 110.08) (Ord. 95-443, passed 11-21-1995) Penalty, see §

Statutory reference:

   No person shall knowingly sell, deliver, or furnish alcoholic beverages to
an intoxicated person or to any person who has been adjudged insane or mentally
deficient.
(Prior Code, § 110.09) (Ord. 95-443, passed 11-21-1995) Penalty, see §
110.99
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see 37A O.S. § 6-121
§ 110.10 PUBLIC INTOXICATION; DRINKING INTOXICATING LIQUOR IN PUBLIC.
   It is unlawful for any person who is drunk or in a state of intoxication to
appear or be upon or in any street, alley, or other public place, or for any
person to drink intoxicating liquor or beverage upon or in any street, alley,
or other public place within the city.
(Prior Code, § 110.10) (Ord. 95-443, passed 11-21-1995) Penalty, see §
110.99
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see 37A O.S. § 6-101A.8
§ 110.11 ADOPTION OF STATE LAWS.
   In addition to the foregoing restrictions, the provisions of the state law
regarding the sale, possession, manufacture, distribution, or use of any
alcoholic beverages, including, without limitation, 37A O.S. §§ 1-101 et seq.,
are hereby adopted and incorporated herein by reference and are enforceable by
the city within the city limits as fully as if set out at length herein and any
violation thereof is punishable in the Municipal Court, the same as violation
of any other city ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 110.11) (Ord. 95-443, passed 11-21-1995)
§ 110.12 GATHERINGS WHERE MINORS ARE CONSUMING ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      ALCOHOL. Ethyl alcohol, hydrated oxide of ethyl, or spirits of wine, from
whatever source or by whatever process produced.
      ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGE. Includes alcohol, spirits, liquor, wine, beer, and
every liquid or solid containing alcohol, spirits, wine, or beer, and which
contains 0.5% or more of alcohol by volume and which is fit for beverage
purposes either alone or when diluted, mixed or combined with other substances.
This term includes intoxicating beverages and low-point beer as defined herein.
      GATHERING. A party, gathering, or event where a group of three or more
persons have assembled or are assembling for a social occasion or social
activity.
      INTOXICATING BEVERAGE. Includes beverages containing more than 3.2%
alcohol by weight.
      LEGAL GUARDIAN.
         (a)   A person who, by court order, is the guardian of the person of a
minor; or
         (b)   A public or private agency with whom a minor has been placed by
the Court.
      LOW-POINT BEER. Includes beverages containing more than 0.5% alcohol by
volume, and not more than 3.2% alcohol by weight, including, but not limited
to, beer or cereal malt beverages obtained by the alcoholic fermentation of an
infusion of barley or other grain, malt, or similar products.
      MINOR. Any person under 21 years of age.
      PARENT. A person who is a natural parent, adoptive parent, foster parent,
or stepparent of another person.
      PREMISES. Any residence or other private property, place, or premises,
including any commercial or business premises.
      RESPONSE COSTS. The costs associated with responses by law enforcement,
fire, and other emergency response providers to a gathering, including, but not
limited to:
         (a)   Salaries and benefits of law enforcement, code enforcement,
fire, or other emergency response personnel for the amount of time spent
responding to, remaining at, or otherwise dealing with a gathering, and the
administrative costs attributable to such response(s);
         (b)   The cost of any medical treatment for any law enforcement, code
enforcement, fire, or other emergency response personnel injured responding to,
remaining at, or leaving the scene of a gathering;
         (c)   The cost of repairing any city equipment or property damaged,
and the cost of the use of any such equipment, in responding to, remaining at
or leaving the scene of a gathering; and
         (d)   Any other allowable costs related to the enforcement of this
section.
   (B)   Consumption of alcohol by minor in public place, place open to public,
or place not open to public. Except as permitted by state law, it is unlawful
for any minor to:
      (1)   Consume at any public place or any place open to the public
alcoholic beverage; or
      (2)   Consume at any place not open to the public any alcoholic beverage,
unless in connection with the consumption of the alcoholic beverage, that minor
is being supervised by his or her parent or legal guardian.
   (C)   Hosting, permitting, or allowing a party, gathering, or event where
minors consuming alcoholic beverages prohibited.
      (1)   It is the duty of any person having control of any premises, who
knowingly hosts, permits, or allows a gathering at said premises, to take all
reasonable steps to prevent the consumption of alcoholic beverages by any minor
at such gathering. Reasonable steps in preventing the consumption of alcoholic
beverages by any minor at such gatherings shall include, but are not limited
to, the following:
         (a)   Controlling access to alcoholic beverages at such gathering;
         (b)   Controlling the quantity of alcoholic beverages present at such
gathering;
         (c)   Verifying the age of persons attending such gathering by
inspecting drivers’ licenses or other government-issued identification cards to
ensure that minors do not consume alcoholic beverages while at the gathering;
and
         (d)   Supervising the activities of minors at the gathering.
      (2)   It is unlawful for any person having control of any premises to
host, permit, or allow a gathering to take place at such premises whenever such
person knows or should have known that the consumption of alcohol by any minor
has occurred.
      (3)   Nothing in this section should be interpreted to prohibit any
religious practice which includes the use of alcohol; however, if a minor
leaves such a religious gathering intoxicated and is found to be in public then
said providers of alcohol will be held responsible in the same manner as a non-
religious gathering.
      (4)   This section shall not apply to any premises licensed by the state
to dispense alcoholic beverages.
      (5)   The city may seek administrative fees and response costs associated
with enforcement of this section through all remedies or procedures provided by
statute, ordinance, or law. This section shall not limit the authority of peace
officers or private citizens to make arrests for any criminal offense arising
out of conduct regulated by this section, nor shall they limit the city’s
ability to initiate and prosecute any criminal offense arising out of the same
circumstances necessitating the application of this section.
      (6)   This section shall not apply where prohibited or preempted by state
or federal law.
(Prior Code, § 110.12) (Ord. 2008-506, passed 11-18-2008) Penalty, see §
110.99
LOW-POINT BEER
§ 110.25 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purposes of this subchapter, all words, phrases, and terms used in
this subchapter and not defined herein shall be interpreted and construed in
conformity with the definitions of the same set forth in 37A O.S. § 1-103, with
the same force and effect as if set forth in full herein, and such definitions
are made a part hereof by reference.
(Prior Code, § 110.25) (Ord. 95-443, passed 11-21-1995)
Statutory reference:
   State law definitions, low-point beer, see 37A O.S. § 1-103
§ 110.26 LICENSE FOR RETAIL SALE.
   (A)   It is unlawful for any retail dealer, whether permanent or temporary
at any place within the limits of the city, to sell, distribute, or dispense
any low-point beer without having first applied for and received a license from
the City Clerk. The annual fee for such a license shall be an amount to be set
by the City Council from time to time for a retail dealer selling low-point
beer for consumption on and off the premises, and another amount to be set by
the City Council from time to time for a retail dealer selling low-point beer
in original packages and not for consumption on the premises. Such fee shall be
paid to the City Clerk at the time of issuance of the license.
   (B)   No license shall be issued under this section without a satisfactory
showing that the applicant has obtained all state and county permits required
by law, and has in all other respects complied with the laws of the state
relating to the sale and distribution of low-point beer. All licenses issued
under this section shall expire on June 30 of each year. No such license shall
be transferable.
   (C)   For the purposes of this section, the term RETAIL DEALER means and
includes any and all persons, firms, corporations, associations, or
concessionaires who sell, distribute, or dispense, at retail, any low-point
beer within the city, without regard as to any place where such beverages may
be consumed or used.
(Prior Code, § 110.26) (Ord. 95-443, passed 11-21-1995) Penalty, see §
110.99
Statutory reference:
   Authority of city to impose above license fee, see 37A O.S. § 4-104
§ 110.27 ON-PREMISES SALE PROHIBITED NEAR SCHOOL OR CHURCH.
   It is unlawful for any person to locate, operate, or maintain any tavern or
other place where low-point beer is sold or dispensed, for consumption on the
premises, within 300 feet of any school or any church located within the city
limits of the city.
(Prior Code, § 110.27) (Ord. 95-443, passed 11-21-1995) Penalty, see §
110.99
§ 110.28 ON-PREMISES SALE PROHIBITED BETWEEN CERTAIN HOURS.
   It shall be unlawful for any place licensed to sell beverages containing
more than 0.5% of alcohol by volume and not more than 3.2% of alcohol be weight
to sell, dispense, or serve such beverages for consumption on the premises
between the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 7:00 a.m. or allow such beverages to be
consumed on the premises between the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 7:00 a.m. excepting
Saturday nights when such beverages may not be sold, dispensed, served, or
consumed on the premises between the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 12:00 p.m. on
Sundays.
(Prior Code, § 110.28) (Ord. 95-443, passed 11-21-1995) Penalty, see §
110.99
Statutory reference:
   On-premises sale prohibited between certain hours, 37A O.S. § 3-125
§ 110.29 SALE TO MINORS; CONSUMPTION BY MINORS.
   It is unlawful for any person who holds a license to sell and dispense beer
or any agent, servant, or employee of the license holder to sell, barter, or
give to any person under 21 years of age any low-point beer. No person under 21
years of age shall consume low-point beer as defined in this subchapter, in any
public place.
(Prior Code, § 110.29) (Ord. 95-443, passed 11-21-1995) Penalty, see §
110.99
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see 37A O.S. §§ 6-101, 6-120
§ 110.30 EMPLOYMENT OF MINORS.
   It is unlawful for any minor to be employed or permitted to work, in any
capacity whatsoever, in a place where low-point beer is sold or dispensed for
consumption on the premises. A parent as regards the employment of his or her
own child or children is excepted from this provision; however, such employment
shall in no capacity whatsoever be related to the selling or dispensing of such
beverages. The provisions of this section shall not apply to any business or
establishment where sales of the beverages do not exceed 25% of the gross sales
of the business or establishment.
(Prior Code, § 110.30) (Ord. 95-443, passed 11-21-1995) Penalty, see §
110.99
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, 37A O.S. §§ 2-121, 6-102
§ 110.31 ADOPTION OF STATE LAWS.
   In addition to the foregoing restrictions, the provisions of the state law
regarding the sale, possession, manufacture, distribution, or use of any
alcoholic beverages, including, without limitation, 37A O.S. §§ 1-101 et seq.,
are hereby adopted and incorporated herein by reference and are enforceable by
the city within the city limits as fully as if set out at length herein and any
violation thereof is punishable in the Municipal Court, the same as violation
of any other city ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 110.31) (Ord. 95-443, passed 11-21-1995)
§ 110.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   Any person who shall violate the provisions of §
110.12 shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. Upon conviction thereof, such
person shall pay a fine in an amount to be set by the City Council from time to
time, plus court costs.
(Prior Code, § 110.99)
CHAPTER 111: FOOD AND RESTAURANTS
Section
   
111.01   Food service sanitation provisions adopted
   
111.02   Milk provisions adopted
   
111.03   Grades of milk which may be sold
   
111.04   Enforcement by whom
 
   
111.99   Penalty
§ 111.01 FOOD SERVICE SANITATION PROVISIONS ADOPTED.
   (A)   The unabridged form of the latest edition of the United States Public
Health Service Food Service Sanitation Ordinance and Code is hereby adopted and
incorporated in this code by reference.
   (B)   At least one copy of the Sanitation Ordinance and Code shall be on
file in the office of the Municipal Clerk.
   (C)   The Sanitation Ordinance and Code shall govern the definitions;
inspection of food service establishments; the issuance, suspension, and
revocation of permits to operate food service establishments; the prohibiting
of the sale of adulterated or misbranded food or drink and the enforcement of
this section.
   (D)   In the Sanitation Ordinance and Code, however, all parenthetical
phrases referring to grading and the following subsections shall be understood
to be deleted: Subsection H.2.e., H.7. and H.8. HEALTH AUTHORITY shall mean the
Director of the County Health Department or his or her designated
representative.
(Prior Code, § 111.01) Penalty, see §
111.99
Statutory reference:
   State food regulations, see 63 O.S. 1-1101 et seq.
§ 111.02 MILK PROVISIONS ADOPTED.
   The production, transportation, processing, handling, sampling, examination,
grading, labeling and sale of all milk and milk products sold for the ultimate
consumption within the city, or its police jurisdiction; the inspection of
dairy herds, dairy farms, and milk plants; the issuing and revocation of
permits to milk producers, haulers, and distributors shall be regulated in
accordance with the provisions
of the Milk Ordinance - Recommendations of the Public Health Service Revised to
Comply with Oklahoma State Statutes, a copy of which shall be filed in the
office of the City Clerk. Sections 9 and 16 of the unabridged ordinance shall
be replaced, respectively by §§
111.03 and
111.04.
(Prior Code, § 111.02)
Statutory reference:
   State regulations on milk and milk products, see 2 O.S. §§ 7-21 et seq. and
§§ 7-401 et seq.
§ 111.03 GRADES OF MILK WHICH MAY BE SOLD.
   Only certified pasteurized and Grade A pasteurized, and certified raw or
Grade A raw milk and milk products shall be sold to the final consumer, or to
restaurants, soda fountains, grocery stores, or similar establishments;
however, in an emergency, the sale of pasteurized milk and milk products which
have not been graded, or the grade of which is unknown, may be authorized by
the health authority; in which case, such milk and milk products shall be
labeled “ungraded.”
(Prior Code, § 111.03)
§ 111.04 ENFORCEMENT BY WHOM.
   All sampling, examining, grading, and regrading of milk and milk products
and all inspections, and issuing and suspension of, revocation of permits shall
be done by the Director of the County Health Department or his or her
authorized representative, who shall be a registered professional sanitarian.
(Prior Code, § 111.04)
§ 111.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)    Any person who violates any of the provisions of §
111.01 shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be
punished as provided in §
10.99. In addition thereto, any person convicted of violation may be enjoined
from continuing the violation.
(Prior Code, § 111.01)
